<div id="review_108220376" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/108220376" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3145375-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1380777905p2/3145375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/108220376?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/3145375-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3145375-nicole?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer108220376" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10636968805930967828">This is the 3rd installment in Karen Chance’s Cassandra Palmer series. It follows Cassie as the newly anointed “Pythia”, also known as the world’s most powerful clairvoyant, as she searches for a counter spell to a curse placed on her when she was a child. I won’t go any further into the plot in this book because without fully explaining the first two books, it would just be too confusing. It suffices to say that there are a lot of people working against Cassie in one way or another and she has </span>
  <span id="freeText10636968805930967828" style="display:none">This is the 3rd installment in Karen Chance’s Cassandra Palmer series. It follows Cassie as the newly anointed “Pythia”, also known as the world’s most powerful clairvoyant, as she searches for a counter spell to a curse placed on her when she was a child. I won’t go any further into the plot in this book because without fully explaining the first two books, it would just be too confusing. It suffices to say that there are a lot of people working against Cassie in one way or another and she has trouble knowing who to trust.<br />As I mentioned above, these books are extremely intricate plots involving no less than thirty or so involved characters, with more appearing around every bend in Cassie’s confusing journey. This has been my chief complaint about these books since I started reading them. <br />That being said, I love the way the relationship between Cassie and Pritkin has developed as Cassie has chipped away at his defenses. Pritkin is a terribly complex character and Chance has been slowly peeling back his layers like a really stinky onion, complete with the watery eyes.<br />Chance writes male characters really well. She makes them sexy and tough, but with a vulnerability that only Cassie seems to bring out. Mircea is no exception. It is refreshing to read a book where there are two equally likely potential suitors, yet the love triangle is not overtly obvious.<br />Overall, this is another enjoyable read from Chance. I look forward to the next installment of the Cassie Palmer series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10636968805930967828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Julie (jjmachshev)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie (jjmachshev)" href="/user/show/882708-julie-jjmachshev">Julie (jjmachshev)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/882708-julie-jjmachshev?shelf=2008-reads">2008-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18449157" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9939841951295615627">The 3rd (final?) book in the Cassie Palmer series from Karen Chance.<br/><br/>Cassandra thought she'd just been in the wrong place at the wrong time...turns out tho, that her being made Pythia was actually the culmination of some truly long-range planning. I really enjoyed the first two books in this series and was waiting anxiously for this one. I enjoyed the book and must give kudos to the author for weaving a complex tale. She did a great job of weaving together the threads that had been cast in the fi</span>
  <span id="freeText9939841951295615627" style="display:none">The 3rd (final?) book in the Cassie Palmer series from Karen Chance.<br /><br />Cassandra thought she'd just been in the wrong place at the wrong time...turns out tho, that her being made Pythia was actually the culmination of some truly long-range planning. I really enjoyed the first two books in this series and was waiting anxiously for this one. I enjoyed the book and must give kudos to the author for weaving a complex tale. She did a great job of weaving together the threads that had been cast in the first two books. I was breathless when I finished.<br /><br />Cassie, as Pythia, can travel through time. Unfortunately, she never got any training and if there was a manual...well, let's just say that apparently nobody wants her to have one. Instead, it seems that all the people she meets just want her to trust them to tell her what she needs to do. The problem with that is she's not sure who, if anyone, she can trust. Cassie is involved with vampires, demons, faeries, talking skulls, magic books...well, the list is really endless.<br /><br />But this is not a mindless tale of love. Everything is not laid out plainly--the intricacies of actions taken while traveling back in time are brought home in this final book. I can't say much else without giving away too much. I will say that I'm not sorry I read these three books and I hope the author will give us future glimpses into Cassie's world.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9939841951295615627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer689360978" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3758432304998052190">I like this series, but there are a few things that irratate me and stop me from loving it. <br/><br/>1. Mircea's character. After reading the Dorina Basarab series I thought he was amazing and wanted to read his and cassies story. But it just doesnt seem like the same character, hes so much more developed in the other series and hes only a secondary character there. Also, I cant stand the geis thing and his relationship with cassie. Pritkin all the way. And mircea should end up with someone else, whos st</span>
  <span id="freeText3758432304998052190" style="display:none">I like this series, but there are a few things that irratate me and stop me from loving it. <br /><br />1. Mircea's character. After reading the Dorina Basarab series I thought he was amazing and wanted to read his and cassies story. But it just doesnt seem like the same character, hes so much more developed in the other series and hes only a secondary character there. Also, I cant stand the geis thing and his relationship with cassie. Pritkin all the way. And mircea should end up with someone else, whos strong enough to stand up for herself. Please let there be a spin off series with him at the center of it, caus in this one he still feels like a secondary character.<br /><br />2. The time travel thing is a bit confusing, I think ive figured it out and then Chance changes the rules again. <br /><br />3. The way Cassie literally stumbles from one crazy situation to another. I love a breakneck pace in a book but this is just ridiculous, it didnt really feel like it made a lot of sense. Plus the way shes just thrown from one situation to the next makes it seem like she doesnt actually try and do anything, and that shes just on the defensive all the time.<br /><br />4. Shes had the power long enough, please let her get some training! Or at least realise how to use it.<br /><br />Other than that good series. Cassie and Pritkin forever ;) and Mircea and some other vampire chick. (maybe the consul?)</span>

<div id="review_349703312" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/349703312" />
    <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder"><img alt="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572373103p2/3048260.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/349703312?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*" href="/user/show/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder">Erin *Proud Book Hoarder*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=ghosts">ghosts</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=magic-powers">magic-powers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=demons">demons</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer349703312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16284613740308325410">This one was superior to the first two. That seems to be a trend with Urban Fantasy books. There is still plenty of action and a lot of time travel, and even though I’m not a fan of time travel, I’ve finally realized the inevitable – it’s a major part of her power, and therefore the story, so it’s not going anywhere.<br/><br/>The second wrapped up with a minor cliffhanger development with the geas. This book focuses full frontal force on that plot line. It’s a pretty major deal for the vampire Mircea and </span>
  <span id="freeText16284613740308325410" style="display:none">This one was superior to the first two. That seems to be a trend with Urban Fantasy books. There is still plenty of action and a lot of time travel, and even though I’m not a fan of time travel, I’ve finally realized the inevitable – it’s a major part of her power, and therefore the story, so it’s not going anywhere.<br /><br />The second wrapped up with a minor cliffhanger development with the geas. This book focuses full frontal force on that plot line. It’s a pretty major deal for the vampire Mircea and Cassandra. Not only to save his sanity and eventually his life, but her own as well, and to clean away any dangers from the Circle and the Senate because of her involvement. It may not be her fault and it may not be fair, but it’s just something the poor girl has to fix. Or else.<br /><br />Cassandra is a little silly with some of her actions and not always the smartest cookie, but she’s likeable as a sympathetic, independent, and non-bitchy heroine. She has horrible luck and it’s just funny. Her power is clever, even if a little weak seeming with all the limitations on it.<br /><br />Pritkin as the war mage and now mentor has softened toward her and realized she’s not the evil incarnate he originally thought. His scenes with Cassie are now much more enjoyable and I like their banter. There is a major revelation about him in this book, and this spicy tidbit makes the story that much more interesting. There’s so many directions that can go. I wasn’t crazy about the flashback scene with him but there was a whopper there. He’s a character who has certainly grown on me.<br /><br />Mircea is around to a degree, but mainly in a weakened, hear about sense. There is an incredibly hot scene between him and Cassie that made my heart speed up dramatically to where I just HAD to keep reading past my bedtime. He’s definitely an interesting character and yummy to boot. <br /><br />This one has as much action as the others, and it’s still confusing to a degree, but it’s staked enough interest in characters to where I’m hooked and really wanting to know what ends up happening to everyone. The start opens with the issue at hand from where the second left off and doesn’t let up on it’s frantic rush to a satisfying finale that wraps up the issue and solves it. Thankfully. I dislike if a story drags something like that on too much. <br /><br />Karen Chance writes action scenes well, even if they are a bit too long. Her dialogue skills are excellent, especially for humor and convincing lines, but sometimes exclamation marks are overused. The world she’s created is complex for the society, time travel and its implications, and future potentials of all kinds of disasters merging with today’s Urban Fantasy creatures and yesterday’s mythology.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16284613740308325410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_15892425" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15892425" />
    <a title="Theresa " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/925476-theresa"><img alt="Theresa " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420405647p2/925476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15892425?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Theresa " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Theresa " href="/user/show/925476-theresa">Theresa </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/925476-theresa?shelf=time-travel">time-travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/925476-theresa?shelf=2008">2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/925476-theresa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15892425" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9905146094740130725">The third entry in the Cassandra Palmer Series, <i>Embrace the Night</i>, kept me enthralled until the last word. What an incredible adventure this book was - I was breathless throughout! <br/><br/>First, let me say that the Cassandra Palmer series has been one of my favorite series since I read the first book.<br/><br/>The author, Karen Chance, wrapped up a bunch of open storylines in this book, but left some big ones open as well for future books in the series. The book has wonderful character development and continuity</span>
  <span id="freeText9905146094740130725" style="display:none">The third entry in the Cassandra Palmer Series, <i>Embrace the Night</i>, kept me enthralled until the last word. What an incredible adventure this book was - I was breathless throughout! <br /><br />First, let me say that the Cassandra Palmer series has been one of my favorite series since I read the first book.<br /><br />The author, Karen Chance, wrapped up a bunch of open storylines in this book, but left some big ones open as well for future books in the series. The book has wonderful character development and continuity from the first two books. <br /><br />The jumping back and forth in time didn't confuse me, but I suppose it could confuse some people. I love books with time travel in them, but sometimes I get irritated when authors ignore paradoxes. This book (and series) tackles time travel paradoxes head on and it was very believably handled. I didn't find any flaws with how the author handled the time travel and its consequent effects. <br /><br />There was a lot of character development for Cassie, Mircea, and Pritkin in this book. There is a lot of history explained for each individual which continued to help to flesh them out. <br /><br />I loved this book and can't wait for the next one in the series! In particular, I can't wait for more Pritkin - I adore his character! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="9905146094740130725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9481759-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550596842p2/9481759.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1304837844?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/9481759-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1304837844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10495478735817602401">I am really liking this series so far. I find it completely entertaining and surprisingly I'm still not tired of reading about Dante's getting trashed. I should be, I know, but somehow it still makes me laugh reading about it. The only complaint I have is with the time travel. While I enjoyed reading about the different settings/time periods I got caught up in trying to make sense of the logistics of it all, especially as it was used to alter events and change or fix the current situation. I'm n</span>
  <span id="freeText10495478735817602401" style="display:none">I am really liking this series so far. I find it completely entertaining and surprisingly I'm still not tired of reading about Dante's getting trashed. I should be, I know, but somehow it still makes me laugh reading about it. The only complaint I have is with the time travel. While I enjoyed reading about the different settings/time periods I got caught up in trying to make sense of the logistics of it all, especially as it was used to alter events and change or fix the current situation. I'm not sure if it was actually all that confusing, or if it's just me making it more difficult than it actually is, based on my own preconceived notions and overall dislike of anything time travel related. For example every time Cassie went to a different time I would pay extremely close attention to what the characters said, I guess on the lookout for things that didn't quite jibe. Then when I thought there was something I would get extremely irritated only to find that it had been cleared up or explained shortly thereafter. I finally figured out that it wasn't as serious as all that and when I stopped trying to over-analyze everything and stopped trying to make sure i could wrap my head around it all, it really became a fun read. I'm looking forward to the next in the series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10495478735817602401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer184226165" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12620184797455003544">Absolutely loved the book. I know this series started rather slow.I mean action wise it was packed but there was something lacking which nagged me.It seemed like the author was trying to find her footing and I think she has found it.<br/><br/>Cassie is witty clever and interesting.She keeps you entertained.The UF bits are fantastic and more than enough eye candy to keep someone like me happy.There is the obvious love triangle developing which keeps you on your toes.Karen Chance made it extremely difficult</span>
  <span id="freeText12620184797455003544" style="display:none">Absolutely loved the book. I know this series started rather slow.I mean action wise it was packed but there was something lacking which nagged me.It seemed like the author was trying to find her footing and I think she has found it.<br /><br />Cassie is witty clever and interesting.She keeps you entertained.The UF bits are fantastic and more than enough eye candy to keep someone like me happy.There is the obvious love triangle developing which keeps you on your toes.Karen Chance made it extremely difficult to chose sides and I am still not sure if I am firmly Team Pritkin or not. The sex scenes were sizzling hot and the chemistry burns off the pages. Cassie keeps making out with both men within a matter of few hours but you can;t call her easy. This book is abundant in time paradoxes so it should be read with a pinch of salt.Therefore people who like to be technical with what they read should be careful.<br /><br />I could not stop reading this book. This has not happened to me from a long time and I am glad I gave this series a chance as I did not know what I was missing.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pKup8i4ksQxXVVivmRryR0gB3OoijAsXFwokwWF8UvoyV+k/1qUpmgwAnjz9KXVTa9fqweu3mPihdmDSx5+seA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('LqicgBA/y0UvBmXYz5hyuIJdHByfjEbjhrLBtoHR5O24VNxN6L5T03RTo0urq/WsoYsqN1a31QwwzoWlJzIabw==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer15256498849371074266">Karen Chance is the author of two New York Times bestselling series, plus a number of novellas and short stories, all set in the Cassandra Palmer universe. A full-time writer since 2008, she was previously a university history teacher, which comes in handy when writing the time-travel aspect of Cassie’s crazy adventures. She loves Las Vegas, the main setting for her novels, but currently lives in </span>
  <span id="freeText15256498849371074266" style="display:none">Karen Chance is the author of two New York Times bestselling series, plus a number of novellas and short stories, all set in the Cassandra Palmer universe. A full-time writer since 2008, she was previously a university history teacher, which comes in handy when writing the time-travel aspect of Cassie’s crazy adventures. She loves Las Vegas, the main setting for her novels, but currently lives in Florida near her family home. Visit her <a href="http://www.karenchance.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">website</a> or connect with her on Facebook <a href="http://on.fb.me/cassandrapalmerseries" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>
